[or rather quasi-inf. n.] <foreign lang="ar">طِيَرَةٌ</foreign>, the only instance of the kind except <foreign lang="ar">خِيَرَةٌ</foreign>, which is the same in relation to <foreign lang="ar">تَخَيَّرَ</foreign>, (IAth,) <hi rend="ital">He augured evil from it; regarded it as an evil omen.</hi> (S, Msb, K.) The Arabs, when they desired to set about an affair, passed by the places where birds lay upon the ground, and roused them, in order to learn thence whether they should proceed or refrain: but the law forbade this. (Msb.) They augured evil from the croaking of the crow, and from the birds' going towards the left; and in like manner, from the motions of gazelles.                   <hi rend="ital">A flying thing</hi> [<hi rend="ital">whether bird</hi> or <hi rend="ital">insect</hi>]: (Msb, * TA:) pl.   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27460-1" target="طَيْرٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n27454"/></foreign>, (S, Msb, K,) like as <foreign lang="ar">صَحْبٌ</foreign> is pl. of <foreign lang="ar">صَاحِبٌ</foreign>: (S, Msb:) or <foreign lang="ar">طَيْرٌ</foreign> is originally an inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">طَارَ</foreign>: or an epithet contracted from <foreign lang="ar">طَيِّرٌ</foreign>: (TA:) or a quasi-pl. n.; (Mgh, TA;) and this is the most correct opinion: (TA:) [but see, below, a reason for considering it originally an inf. n.:] and <foreign lang="ar">طَائِرٌ</foreign> may also be quasi-pl. n., like <foreign lang="ar">جَامِلٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">بَاقِرٌ</foreign>: (TA:)   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27460-2" target="طَيْرٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n27454"/></foreign> is also sometimes used as a sing.; (Ktr, AO, S, Mgh, Msb, K;) as in the Kur iii. 43 [and v. 110], accord. to one reading: (S:) but ISd says, I know not how this is, unless it be meant to be [originally] an inf. n.: (TA:) [for an inf. n. used as an epithet is employed as sing. and pl.:] or <foreign lang="ar">طَائِرٌ</foreign>, only, is used as a sing., (Th, IAmb, Msb,) by general consent; and AO once said so in common with others: (Th:) but   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27460-3" target="طَيْرٌ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n27454"/></foreign> has a collective, or pl., signification: (IAmb, Msb:) and is fem.: (Mgh:) or is more frequently fem. than masc.: (IAmb, Msb:) the pl. of <foreign lang="ar">طَيْرٌ</foreign> is <foreign lang="ar">طُيُورٌ</foreign> [a pl. of mult.] and <foreign lang="ar">أَطْيَارٌ</foreign> [a pl. of pauc.]: (S, Msb, K:) or <foreign lang="ar">طُيُورٌ</foreign> may be pl. of <foreign lang="ar">طَائِرٌ</foreign>, like as <foreign lang="ar">سُجُودٌ</foreign> is pl. of <foreign lang="ar">سَاجِدٌ</foreign>: (TA:) <foreign lang="ar">طَائِرَةٌ</foreign> is seldom applied to the female. (IAmb, Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [<foreign lang="ar">الطَّائِر</foreign> is a name of <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The constellation Cygnus;</hi> also called <foreign lang="ar">الدَّجَاجَةُ</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ سَاكِنُ الطَّائِرِ</foreign> means <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He is grave, staid, sedate,</hi> (K,) or <hi rend="ital">motionless;</hi> so that if a bird alighted upon him, it would be still; for if a bird alight upon a man, and he move in the least, the bird flies away. (TA.) Of the same kind also is the saying, <foreign lang="ar">رُزِقَ فُلَانٌ سُكُونَ الطَّائِرِ وَخَفْضَ الجِنَاحِ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">Such a one was endowed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">has been endowed, with gravity and gentleness</hi>]. (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">طُيُورُهُمْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">سَوَاكِنُ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">They are remaining fixed, settled,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">at rest:</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">شَالَتْ نَعَامَتُهُمْ</foreign> signifies the contrary. (A, TA.) And   
      <foreign lang="ar">كَأَنَّ عَلَى رُؤُسِهِمُ <ref cref="n27460-4" target="الطَّيْرَ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">As though birds were on their heads</hi>] is said of a people, meaning them to be <hi rend="ital">motionless by reason of reverence:</hi> (S, K:) it was said of the Companions of Mohammad, describing them as quiet and grave [in his presence], without levity: and the origin of the saying is this: that birds alight only upon a thing that is still and inanimate: (TA:) or that the crow alights upon the head of the camel, and picks from it the ticks, (S, K,) and the young ones thereof, (S,) and the camel does not move (S, K) his head, (S,) lest the crow should take fright and fly away. (S, K.) In like manner, <foreign lang="ar">وَقَعَ طَائِرُهُ</foreign> means <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He became grave,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sedate.</hi> (Meyd.) And <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27460-5" target="طَارَ" n="5" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar" select="n27448"/>طَائِرُهُ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He became light,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">inconstant:</hi> (Meyd:) and <hi rend="ital">he became angry;</hi> (O, K, TA;) like <foreign lang="ar">ثَارَ ثَائِرُهُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">فَارَ فَائِرُهُ</foreign>: (TA:) or <hi rend="ital">he hastened, and was light,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">active,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">agile.</hi> (Har p. 561.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  And it is said in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">الرُّؤْيَا عَلَى رِجْلِ طَائِرٍ مَا لَمْ تُعَبَّرْ</foreign> (O, TA) <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">A dream is unsettled as to its result,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">final sequel, while it is not interpreted.</hi> (TA.) [The Arabs hold that the result of a dream is affected by its interpretation: wherefore it is added in this tradition, and said in others also, that the dreamer should not relate his dream, unless to a friend or to a person of understanding.]          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>    
      <foreign lang="ar">عَيَّثَتْ <ref cref="n27460-6" target="طَيْرُهُ" n="6" type="1" subtype="SO" lang="ar"/></foreign> see expl. in art. <foreign lang="ar">عيث</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">طَائِرٌ</foreign> also signifies <hi rend="ital">A thing from which one augurs either good</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evil; an omen, a bodement, of good</hi> or <hi rend="ital">of evil:</hi> (K:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27460-7" target="طِيَرَةٌ" n="7" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> (S, K) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27460-8" target="طِيرَةٌ" n="8" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> (K) and

                  <foreign lang="ar">فَأْلٌ</foreign>: (TA:) and <foreign lang="ar">طَائِرٌ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">fortune,</hi> (A'Obeyd, K, TA,) <hi rend="ital">whether good</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evil:</hi> (TA:) and especially <hi rend="ital">evil fortune; ill luck;</hi> as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27460-10" target="طَيْرٌ" n="10" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n27454"/></foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27460-11" target="طِيَرَةٌ" n="11" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>: for the Arabs used to augur evil from the croaking of the crow, and from birds going towards the left: [see 5:] (TA:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27460-12" target="طِيَرَةٌ" n="12" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> is an inf. n. [or rather a quasi-inf. n.] of <foreign lang="ar">تَطَيَّرَ</foreign>, [q. v.,] (IAth,) and signifies <hi rend="ital">auguration of evil.</hi> (Msb.) The Arabs used to say, to a man or other thing from which they augured evil, (TA,) <foreign lang="ar">طَائِرُ ٱللّٰهِ لَا طَائِرُكَ</foreign>, (ISk, <pb n="1905"/> S, IAmb,) and <foreign lang="ar">طائرَ اللّٰه لا طائرَك</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">What God doth and decreeth, not what thou dost and causest to be feared:</hi> (IAmb:) accord. to ISk, one should not say <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27460-13" target="طَيْرُ" n="13" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>ٱللّٰهِ</foreign>: (S:) but the Arabs are related to have said, also, <foreign lang="ar">لَا طَيْرَ إِلَّا طَيْرُ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">There is no evil fortune but that which is of God</hi>]; like as one says, <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَمْرَ إِلَّا أَمْرُ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign>. (As, S.) They also used to say, <foreign lang="ar">جَرَى لَهُ الطَّائِرُ بِأَمْرِ كَذَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Fortune brought to him such an event</hi>]: and hence fortune, whether good or evil, is called <foreign lang="ar">طائر</foreign>. (TA.) And it is said in the Kur [vii. 128], <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّمَا طَائِرُهُمْ عِنْدَ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Their evil fortune,</hi> which will overtake them, <hi rend="ital">is only</hi> that which is threatened to befall them in the latter state, [<hi rend="ital">with God,</hi>] and not that which befalls them in the present state of existence: (TA:) or <hi rend="ital">the cause of their good and evil is only with God;</hi> i. e., it is his decree and will: or <hi rend="ital">the cause of their evil fortune is only with God;</hi> i. e., it is their works, which are registered with Him. (Bd.) It is said in a trad., that Mohammad liked what is termed <foreign lang="ar">فَأْل</foreign>, and disliked what is termed   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n27460-14" target="طِيَرَة" n="14" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>: (S:) and in another, that he denied there being any such thing as the latter. (TA.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  Also The <hi rend="ital">means of subsistence;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">رِزْقٌ</foreign>. (K:) or <hi rend="ital">misery:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">happiness:</hi> every one of these three significations has been assigned to it in the Kur xvii. 14: in which, accord. to AM, it is meant that God has decreed to every man happiness or misery, according as He foresaw that he would be obedient or disobedient. (TA.) [See also what immediately follows.]       <sense type="A" n="3">-A3-</sense>  Also The <hi rend="ital">actions of a man which are</hi> [<hi rend="ital">as it were</hi>] <hi rend="ital">attached as a necklace to his neck.</hi> (S, Msb, K.)                   </quote> [<hi rend="ital">And to the family of Harráb and Kadd belongs an eminence in glory of which they fear not any diminution:</hi> lit., <hi rend="ital">of which the crow is not made to fly away;</hi> the greatness of their glory being likened to abundant seed-produce, as has been shown above: see 2]: (S:) A 'Obeyd says that Harráb and Kadd were two men of the BenooAsad.
